But Y + ќї v_y = 1.58745 + 0.83333*(-3.1749)=1.58745-2.64575=-1.0583. So Y + ќї v_y = -1.0583. However, E_y - (-y_A) = y_A + ќї v_y - (-y_A) = 2y_A + ќї v_y = Y + ќї v_y. So that is correct. But in our numeric, we computed E_y - (-y_A) = -0.5282745 + 0.7937255 = 0.265451. That is not -1.0583. So there is a mistake: We have y_A = Y/2 = 0.7937255, so 2y_A = Y = 1.58745. Then E_y = y_A + ќї v_y = 0.7937255 + 0.83333*(-3.1749)=0.7937255 -2.64575 = -1.852025? Wait, we computed earlier E = (0.6, -0.5282745). That was from E = A + ќї v, but we used v = (0.6, -1.587451). That gave E = (0.6, -0.5282745). But then y_A = 0.7937255, so E_y should be 0.7937255 + ќї v_y = 0.7937255 + 0.83333*(-1.587451)=0.7937255 -1.322= -0.5282745. That's consistent. So E_y = -0.5282745. Then 2y_A + ќї v_y = 2*0.7937255 + (-1.322) = 1.58745 -1.322 = 0.26545. So that's the correct value. But we also have Y + ќї v_y = 1.58745 + ќї v_y? Wait, ќї v_y = 0.83333*(-1.587451)= -1.322, so Y + ќї v_y = 1.58745 -1.322 = 0.26545. So earlier we said Y + ќї v_y = -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' = -1.0583, but that's wrong. So the expression -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' is not equal to Y + ќї v_y. Let's recalc that derivation.

We had Y + ќї v_y = Y + (2ќФ/(X+ќФ')) * (-Y X/ќФ) = Y - (2X Y)/(X+ќФ') = Y [1 - 2X/(X+ќФ')] = Y [(X+ќФ' - 2X)/(X+ќФ')] = Y [ (ќФ' - X)/(X+ќФ') ] = -Y (X - ќФ')/(X+ќФ'). And X - ќФ' = 2ѕБ, X+ќФ' = 2ѕБ'. So Y + ќї v_y = -Y * (2ѕБ)/(2ѕБ') = -Y ѕБ/ѕБ'. So that gives -Y ѕБ/ѕБ'. But numeric: Y=1.58745, ѕБ=0.8, ѕБ'=1.2, so -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' = -1.58745*0.8/1.2 = -1.58745*0.6667 = -1.0583. But our computed Y + ќї v_y = 0.26545. So clearly, there is a mistake in the substitution: We used ќї = 2ќФ/(X+ќФ')? Let's re-express ќї in terms of ќФ and ќФ'. ќї = ќФ/ѕБ'. And ѕБ' = (X+ќФ')/2? But X = 1+ќФ, so X+ќФ' = 1+ќФ+ќФ' = 2ѕБ'. So ѕБ' = (X+ќФ')/2. Thus, ќї = ќФ / ((X+ќФ')/2) = 2ќФ/(X+ќФ'). So that is correct. Now, v_y = -Y X/ќФ. So ќї v_y = (2ќФ/(X+ќФ')) * (-Y X/ќФ) = -2Y X/(X+ќФ'). Then Y + ќї v_y = Y - 2Y X/(X+ќФ') = Y [1 - 2X/(X+ќФ')] = Y [(X+ќФ' - 2X)/(X+ќФ')] = Y [(ќФ' - X)/(X+ќФ')] = -Y (X-ќФ')/(X+ќФ'). So far correct.

Now, X-ќФ' = (1+ќФ) - ќФ' = 1+ќФ-ќФ'. And ѕБ = (X-ќФ')/2? Since ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2 = (X-ќФ')/2. So X-ќФ' = 2ѕБ. And X+ќФ' = 2ѕБ'. So Y + ќї v_y = -Y * (2ѕБ)/(2ѕБ') = -Y ѕБ/ѕБ'. So that yields -1.0583. But numeric gives Y+ќї v_y = 0.26545. So either Y is not sqrt(ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2))? Let's compute Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) = 1*3*(1-0.16)=3*0.84=2.52, so Y=1.58745. That's fine. Then ѕБ=0.8, ѕБ'=1.2. So -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' = -1.58745*0.8/1.2 = -1.0583. So the expression gives -1.0583. But our numeric from coordinates gave 0.26545. So the numeric from coordinates must be wrong because we used v = (0.6, -1.587451) and ќї=0.83333, so ќї v_y = -1.322, and Y = 1.58745, so Y+ќї v_y = 0.26545. That is correct. So the formula Y+ќї v_y = -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' gives a different number, so the algebra must have a sign error in the derivation of v_y. Let's recompute v_y correctly.

We have P = (p_x, p_y). For this numeric, we have p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2 = (1+1.2-0.8)/2=0.7. p_y = -y_A/ќФ = -0.7937255/1 = -0.7937255. So P = (0.7, -0.7937255). A = (0.1, 0.7937255). Then v = P - A = (0.6, -1.587451). So v_y = -1.587451. That is correct. Now, Y = sqrt(ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)). ќФ=1, ќФ'=0.4, so Y = sqrt(3*0.84)= sqrt(2.52)=1.58745. So Y = 1.58745. Now, v_y = -1.587451. So v_y = -Y? Since Y=1.58745, v_y = -1.58745 = -Y. So v_y = -Y. That is interesting: v_y = -Y. Then ќї v_y = -ќї Y. So Y + ќї v_y = Y - ќї Y = Y(1-ќї). ќї = ќФ/ѕБ' = 1/1.2 = 0.83333, so 1-ќї = 0.16667, then Y(1-ќї)=1.58745*0.16667=0.2646. That matches. Now, using the formula -Y ѕБ/ѕБ' = -Y * 0.8/1.2 = -Y * 0.6667 = -1.0583, which is not equal. So the derivation that gave v_y = -Y X/ќФ is wrong because we used X=1+ќФ=2, ќФ=1, so -Y X/ќФ = -1.58745*2/1 = -3.1749, but actual v_y = -1.58745. So the expression for v_y is not -Y X/ќФ. Let's recalc v_y from the formula: v_y = p_y - y_A. We have p_y = -y_A/ќФ, and y_A = Y/2. So p_y = -Y/(2ќФ). Then v_y = p_y - y_A = -Y/(2ќФ) - Y/2 = -Y(1/(2ќФ) + 1/2) = -Y( (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ) = -Y X/(2ќФ). So v_y = -Y X/(2ќФ). For our numeric, X=2, ќФ=1, so v_y = -Y*2/(2)= -Y = -1.58745. That matches. So the correct expression is v_y = -Y X/(2ќФ). Earlier we had v_y = -Y X/ќФ, missing factor 1/2. So that's the error. Let's correct.

Thus, v = (v_x, v_y) with v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, and v_y = -Y X/(2ќФ). Good.

Now, recompute E-B and F-B with correct v_y.

We have:

A = (x_A, y_A) = ((1 - ќФ' X)/2, Y/2) where X=1+ќФ.
v = (v_x, v_y) = (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y X/(2ќФ)).
ќї = ќФ/ѕБ' = 2ќФ/(X+ќФ').
ќЉ = ќФ/ѕБ = 2ќФ/(X-ќФ').

Then E = A + ќї v, so:

E_x - x_A = ќї v_x = (2ќФ/(X+ќФ')) * (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2) = ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X+ќФ').
E_y - y_A = ќї v_y = (2ќФ/(X+ќФ')) * (-Y X/(2ќФ)) = -Y X/(X+ќФ') = -Y X/(2ѕБ')? Since X+ќФ' = 2ѕБ', so -Y X/(2ѕБ'). Then E_y - (-y_A) = E_y + y_A = (y_A + ќї v_y) + y_A = 2y_A + ќї v_y = Y + ќї v_y. And ќї v_y = -Y X/(X+ќФ') = -Y X/(2ѕБ'). So Y + ќї v_y = Y - Y X/(2ѕБ') = Y [1 - X/(2ѕБ')]. But X = 1+ќФ, ѕБ' = (X+ќФ')/2. So X/(2ѕБ') = X/(X+ќФ') = (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ'). So 1 - X/(2ѕБ') = 1 - (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = ( (1+ќФ+ќФ') - (1+ќФ) )/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ'). So Y + ќї v_y = Y * ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = Y * ќФ'/(X+ќФ') = Y * ќФ'/(2ѕБ')? Actually, X+ќФ' = 2ѕБ', so ќФ'/(X+ќФ') = ќФ'/(2ѕБ'). So E-B = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X+ќФ'), Y ќФ'/(2ѕБ')? Wait, Y + ќї v_y = Y ќФ'/(X+ќФ') = Y ќФ'/(2ѕБ'). But we also have the expression from the algebra: E-B = (ќї v_x, Y + ќї v_y). So E-B = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X+ќФ'), Y ќФ'/(X+ќФ')). Good.

Now, F-B: ќЉ v_x = (2ќФ/(X-ќФ')) * (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2) = ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X-ќФ').
ќЉ v_y = (2ќФ/(X-ќФ')) * (-Y X/(2ќФ)) = -Y X/(X-ќФ') = -Y X/(2ѕБ) since X-ќФ' = 2ѕБ. Then Y + ќЉ v_y = Y - Y X/(X-ќФ') = Y [1 - X/(X-ќФ')] = Y [ (X-ќФ' - X)/(X-ќФ') ] = Y (-ќФ')/(X-ќФ') = -Y ќФ'/(2ѕБ). So F-B = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X-ќФ'), -Y ќФ'/(X-ќФ')).

Thus, E-B = ( ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X+ќФ'), Y ќФ'/(X+ќФ') )
F-B = ( ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X-ќФ'), -Y ќФ'/(X-ќФ') )

Now, we also have |B|^2 = ѕБ^2 = (X-ќФ')^2/4. |E|^2 = ѕБ^2, so first equation: O¬Ј(E-B)=0 gives:

O_x * (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X+ќФ')) + O_y * (Y ќФ'/(X+ќФ')) = 0 => multiply by (X+ќФ'): O_x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) + O_y Y ќФ' = 0 => O_x ќФ (2+ќФ) + O_y Y = 0 => O_x ќФ (2+ќФ) = - O_y Y. (Eq1)

Second equation: O¬Ј(F-B) = (|F|^2 - ѕБ^2)/2 = ( (2+ќФ)ќФќФ' / ѕБ )/2 = (2+ќФ)ќФќФ'/(2ѕБ). So:

O_x * (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(X-ќФ')) + O_y * ( -Y ќФ'/(X-ќФ') ) = (2+ќФ)ќФќФ'/(2ѕБ). Multiply both sides by (X-ќФ'):

O_x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) - O_y Y ќФ' = (2+ќФ)ќФќФ' (X-ќФ')/(2ѕБ). But (X-ќФ')/(2ѕБ) = 1? Since ѕБ = (X-ќФ')/2, so (X-ќФ')/(2ѕБ) = 1. So right side becomes (2+ќФ)ќФќФ'. So we have:

O_x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) - O_y Y ќФ' = (2+ќФ)ќФќФ'. Divide both sides by ќФќФ' (nonzero): O_x (2+ќФ) - O_y Y/ќФ = (2+ќФ)/ќФ? Wait, careful: We have O_x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) - O_y Y ќФ' = (2+ќФ)ќФќФ'. Cancel ќФќФ': O_x (2+ќФ) - O_y Y/ќФ = (2+ќФ). So O_x (2+ќФ) = (2+ќФ) + O_y Y/ќФ. Thus, O_x = 1 + O_y Y/(ќФ (2+ќФ)). (Eq2)

Now, from Eq1: O_x ќФ (2+ќФ) = - O_y Y => O_x = - O_y Y / (ќФ (2+ќФ)). Plug into Eq2:

- O_y Y / (ќФ (2+ќФ)) = 1 + O_y Y/(ќФ (2+ќФ)) => bring terms: - O_y Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) - O_y Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) = 1 => -2 O_y Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) = 1 => O_y = - ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y). So O_y = - (2+ќФ)ќФ/(2Y). Then O_x = - O_y Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) = - [ - (2+ќФ)ќФ/(2Y) ] * Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) = ( (2+ќФ)ќФ/(2Y) ) * Y/(ќФ(2+ќФ)) = 1/2. So O_x = 1/2.

Thus, the circumcenter O_BEF is (1/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y)). That is (0.5, -0.945). Good! So the correct O is (1/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y)). And we have derived that O_x = 1/2, independent of parameters. That is a very nice result. So O_BEF = (1/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y)). And radius R = distance from O to B. B = (x_A, -y_A). But we also know that |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2 = |O-F|^2. So R = |O-B|.

Now, we need to prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circle (BEF). We have H = (p_x, p_y - p_x(1-p_x)/p_y?) Actually, we have H = (p_x, p_x(1-p_x)/p_y). But p_x = (1+ќФ')/2, and p_y = -y_A/ќФ = -Y/(2ќФ). So p_x(1-p_x) = (1-ќФ'^2)/4. Then H = ((1+ќФ')/2, - (1-ќФ'^2)/(4) * ќФ / Y? Actually, p_x(1-p_x)/p_y = ((1-ќФ'^2)/4) / (-Y/(2ќФ)) = ((1-ќФ'^2)/4) * (-2ќФ/Y) = -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y). So H = ((1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y)). 

Now, direction vector v = AP = P-A = (v_x, v_y) = (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y X/(2ќФ)). And we have X=1+ќФ.

Thus, v = ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ).

Now, the line L: H + t v.

We need to show that the distance from O to L equals R. That is, |(O-H) √Ч v| / |v| = R.

We have O = (1/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y)). Compute O-H:

O_x - H_x = 1/2 - (1+ќФ')/2 = -ќФ'/2.
O_y - H_y = -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y) - ( -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) ) = -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y) + ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) = ќФ/(2Y) [ - (2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2) ] = ќФ/(2Y) [ -2-ќФ +1 -ќФ'^2 ] = ќФ/(2Y) [ -1 -ќФ -ќФ'^2 ] = -ќФ(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)/(2Y). So O-H = ( -ќФ'/2, -ќФ(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)/(2Y) ).

Now, v = ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ). Compute cross product (det) D = (O-H)_x * v_y - (O-H)_y * v_x.

(O-H)_x = -ќФ'/2, v_y = -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ). So first term = (-ќФ'/2) * (-Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)) = ќФ' Y (1+ќФ)/(4ќФ).
(O-H)_y = -ќФ(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)/(2Y), v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2. So second term = ( -ќФ(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)/(2Y) ) * ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2 ) = -ќФ ќФ' (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(4Y). Then D = first term - second term = ќФ' Y (1+ќФ)/(4ќФ) - ( -ќФ ќФ' (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(4Y) ) = ќФ' Y (1+ќФ)/(4ќФ) + ќФ ќФ' (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(4Y).

Factor ќФ'/4: D = (ќФ'/4) [ Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y ].

Now, |v|^2 = v_x^2+v_y^2 = (ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2)/4 + (Y^2 (1+ќФ)^2)/(4ќФ^2). Using Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So v_y^2 = (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) (1+ќФ)^2)/(4ќФ^2) = (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/(4ќФ). Thus, |v|^2 = (2+ќФ)/4 [ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ ] = (2+ќФ)/4 * T, where T = ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ. But we earlier simplified T = ( (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 )/ќФ? Let's verify: We had earlier T = ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ = ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ) + (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ - ќФ'^2 (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ = ќФ'^2 [ (2+ќФ) - (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ ] + (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ. Compute (2+ќФ) - (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ = (2+ќФ) - (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2)/ќФ = (2+ќФ) - (1/ќФ + 2 + ќФ) = 2+ќФ -1/ќФ -2 -ќФ = -1/ќФ. So T = ќФ'^2 * (-1/ќФ) + (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ = ( (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 )/ќФ = ( (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 )/ќФ. That is correct. So |v|^2 = (2+ќФ)/4 * ( (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 )/ќФ = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ). But ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2) = (1+ќФ-ќФ')(1+ќФ+ќФ') = (2ѕБ)(2ѕБ') = 4ѕБѕБ'. So |v|^2 = (2+ќФ)(4ѕБѕБ')/(4ќФ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ. That matches earlier.

Now, compute R^2 = |O-B|^2. O = (1/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y)), B = (x_A, -y_A) = ((1-ќФ'X)/2, -Y/2). So O-B = (1/2 - (1-ќФ'X)/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y) + Y/2) = ( (1 - (1-ќФ'X))/2, (Y/2 - ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y) ) = ( ќФ'X/2, (Y^2 - ќФ(2+ќФ))/(2Y) ). Now, Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So Y^2 - ќФ(2+ќФ) = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2 - 1) = -ќФ(2+ќФ)ќФ'^2. Thus, O-B = ( ќФ'X/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)ќФ'^2/(2Y) ) = ( ќФ'X/2, -ќФќФ'^2(2+ќФ)/(2Y) ). Then R^2 = (ќФ'X/2)^2 + (ќФќФ'^2(2+ќФ)/(2Y))^2 = ќФ'^2 X^2/4 + ќФ^2 ќФ'^4 (2+ќФ)^2/(4Y^2) = ќФ'^2/4 [ X^2 + ќФ^2 ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / Y^2 ]. But Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So ќФ^2 ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / Y^2 = ќФ^2 ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)) = ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2). So R^2 = ќФ'^2/4 [ X^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ]. Now, X = 1+ќФ, so X^2 = (1+ќФ)^2. So R^2 = ќФ'^2/4 [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ].

Now, we also have D = (ќФ'/4) * S, where S = Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y. So |D| = |ќФ'/4| * |S|. Since ќФ'>0, S>0 likely. So the distance from O to L is |D|/|v| = (ќФ'/4 * S) / |v|. So we need to show that this equals R.

Thus, we need:

(ќФ'/4 * S) / |v| = R => ќФ' S / (4 |v|) = R => S = 4 R |v| / ќФ'.

Now, compute R |v|: R = sqrt( ќФ'^2/4 [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ] ) = (ќФ'/2) sqrt( (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ). |v| = sqrt( (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ ) = sqrt( (2+ќФ) * ( (X-ќФ')/2 * (X+ќФ')/2 ) / ќФ ) = sqrt( (2+ќФ) * (X^2-ќФ'^2)/4 / ќФ ) = sqrt( (2+ќФ)(X^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) ). Since X=1+ќФ, X^2-ќФ'^2 = (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2. So |v| = sqrt( (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) ). So R |v| = (ќФ'/2) sqrt( (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ) * sqrt( (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) ) = (ќФ'/2) sqrt( ( (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ) * ( (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) ) ). This is messy.

But we can compute S and see if S = 4 R |v|/ќФ'. Alternatively, we can compute the distance squared from O to L directly and compare to R^2. That is, we need to show that (|D|^2)/(|v|^2) = R^2. That is, D^2 = R^2 |v|^2.

We have D = (ќФ'/4) S. So D^2 = (ќФ'^2/16) S^2. And R^2 |v|^2 = R^2 * (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ =? But we can also compute R^2 |v|^2 directly from the expressions we have for R^2 and |v|^2.

We have R^2 = ќФ'^2/4 [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ].
|v|^2 = (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ = (2+ќФ)((X-ќФ')/2 * (X+ќФ')/2)/ќФ = (2+ќФ)(X^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ).

Thus, R^2 |v|^2 = ќФ'^2/4 * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ] * (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) = ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(16ќФ) * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ].

So we need to show that (ќФ'^2/16) S^2 = ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/(16ќФ) * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ]. Cancel ќФ'^2/16 (assuming ќФ'>0): we need S^2 = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ].

Now, S = Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y. Recall Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So we can write S in terms of Y. Let's compute S^2 and see if it matches the right side.

Compute S^2 = [Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y]^2 = [ (Y^2 (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) ) / Y ]^2 = [ (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) ) / Y ]^2 = [ ( (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) ) / Y ]^2 = [ (2+ќФ) ( (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) ) / Y ]^2.

So S^2 = (2+ќФ)^2 / Y^2 * [ (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) ]^2. And Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So S^2 = (2+ќФ)^2 / (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)) * [ ... ]^2 = (2+ќФ) / (ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)) * [ (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) ]^2.

Thus, S^2 = (2+ќФ) / (ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)) * [ (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) ]^2.

Now, the right side we need is: RHS = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ].

Let's denote A = (1+ќФ)^2, B = ќФ'^2. Then:

(1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 = A - B.
(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) = A? Not, A = (1+ќФ)^2 = 1+2ќФ+ќФ^2. And (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) = 1+ќФ+ќФ'^2. That's different.

Also, (1-ќФ'^2) = 1 - B.

Then S^2 = (2+ќФ)/(ќФ(1-B)) * [ (1-B)A + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2.

RHS = (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

We need to check if these are equal. This is an identity in ќФ and B (with B<1). We can attempt to verify by expanding both sides. Let's do that.

LetвАЩs define:

S^2 = (2+ќФ)/(ќФ(1-B)) * [ A(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2.

RHS = (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

Cancel (2+ќФ)/ќФ common factor? Actually, S^2 has factor (2+ќФ)/(ќФ(1-B)), RHS has factor (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ. So multiply both sides by ќФ/(2+ќФ) to get:

S^2 * ќФ/(2+ќФ) = 1/(1-B) * [ A(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2.
RHS * ќФ/(2+ќФ) = (A-B) * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

Thus, we need to show:

1/(1-B) * [ A(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2 = (A-B) * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

Multiply both sides by (1-B):

[ A(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2 = (A-B)(1-B) * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ] = (A-B)(1-B)A + (A-B)ќФ B (2+ќФ).

But note that (A-B)(1-B)A = A(A-B)(1-B). And (A-B)ќФ B (2+ќФ) = ќФ B (A-B)(2+ќФ). So RHS = A(A-B)(1-B) + ќФ B (A-B)(2+ќФ). Now, left side: LHS = [ A(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2.

We need to verify this identity. Let's expand both sides in terms of ќФ and B. Since A = (1+ќФ)^2 = 1+2ќФ+ќФ^2.

Compute LHS = [ (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2)(1-B) + ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+B) ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2)(1-B) + ќФ^2 + ќФ^3 + ќФ^2 B ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2)(1-B) + ќФ^2 + ќФ^3 + ќФ^2 B ]^2. Now, (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2)(1-B) = (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2) - B(1+2ќФ+ќФ^2). So LHS = [ (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2) - B(1+2ќФ+ќФ^2) + ќФ^2 + ќФ^3 + ќФ^2 B ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2+ќФ^2+ќФ^3) + B( -1-2ќФ-ќФ^2 + ќФ^2) ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ+2ќФ^2+ќФ^3) + B( -1-2ќФ) ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ+2ќФ^2+ќФ^3) - B(1+2ќФ) ]^2 = [ (1+2ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ^2) - B(1+2ќФ) ]^2? Actually, 1+2ќФ+2ќФ^2+ќФ^3 = (1+2ќФ) + ќФ^2(2+ќФ) = (1+2ќФ) + ќФ^2(2+ќФ). Not factorable simply. But note that (1+2ќФ) = (1+ќФ)+ќФ? Not.

Now, RHS = A(A-B)(1-B) + ќФ B (A-B)(2+ќФ). Compute A = (1+ќФ)^2. So RHS = (1+ќФ)^2 ( (1+ќФ)^2 - B ) (1-B) + ќФ B ( (1+ќФ)^2 - B ) (2+ќФ). Expand? This seems heavy but maybe we can show that both sides are equal to ( (1+ќФ)^2 - B ) times something? Let's attempt to compute LHS and RHS for a specific numeric to see if they match. Take ќФ=1, B=0.16. Then:

LHS: Compute inside: A=4, (1-B)=0.84, so A(1-B)=3.36. ќФ^2=1, (1+ќФ+B)=1+1+0.16=2.16, so ќФ^2(1+ќФ+B)=2.16. Sum=5.52. Square=30.4704.
RHS: (A-B)=4-0.16=3.84. (1-B)=0.84, so A(A-B)(1-B)=4*3.84*0.84=4*3.2256=12.9024. ќФ B (A-B)(2+ќФ)=1*0.16*3.84*3=0.16*11.52=1.8432. Sum=14.7456. Not equal. So there is a discrepancy. Did we cancel incorrectly? We had S^2 = (2+ќФ)/(ќФ(1-B)) * [ ... ]^2. Then we multiplied by ќФ/(2+ќФ) to get S^2 * ќФ/(2+ќФ) = 1/(1-B) * [ ... ]^2. Then RHS * ќФ/(2+ќФ) = (A-B) * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ]. So we need:

1/(1-B) * [ ... ]^2 = (A-B) * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

For numeric: ќФ=1, B=0.16, then [ ... ] = A(1-B)+ќФ^2(1+ќФ+B)=4*0.84+1*2.16=3.36+2.16=5.52. So LHS of this reduced equality = (1/0.84)*30.4704 = 36.287. RHS = (A-B)*[A+ќФB(2+ќФ)/(1-B)] = 3.84 * [4 + 1*0.16*3/0.84] = 3.84 * [4 + 0.48/0.84] = 3.84 * [4 + 0.5714] = 3.84 * 4.5714 = 17.55. Not equal. So the equality we need is not satisfied. That means our earlier claim that the distance from O to L equals R might be false? But we previously verified numerically that for this numeric, the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to (BEF) using the direct calculation of distances? Let's recompute that numeric with higher precision.

We have for ќФ=1, ќФ'=0.4, ѕБ=0.8, ѕБ'=1.2, Y= sqrt(2.52)=1.587451. Then:

O = (0.5, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(2Y) = -3/(2*1.587451)= -3/3.174902= -0.945. So O = (0.5, -0.945). B = (0.1, -0.7937255). Distance R = sqrt((0.4)^2 + (0.1512745)^2)= sqrt(0.16+0.02289)= sqrt(0.18289)=0.4277. H = ((1+0.4)/2=0.7, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) = -1*(0.84)/(2*1.587451)= -0.84/3.174902= -0.2647). v = (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2=0.4*3/2=0.6, -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) = -1.587451*2/(2)= -1.587451). So L: H + t v = (0.7+0.6t, -0.2647 -1.58745t). Now compute distance from O to L.

We have O-H = (0.5-0.7=-0.2, -0.945+0.2647=-0.6803). v = (0.6, -1.58745). Cross product: (-0.2)*(-1.58745) - (-0.6803)*0.6 = 0.31749 + 0.40818 = 0.72567. |v| = sqrt(0.36+2.5199)= sqrt(2.8799)=1.697. So distance = 0.72567/1.697 = 0.4276. That is exactly R (0.4277). So the line is tangent. Good.

Now, our algebraic expression for D = (O-H) √Ч v should be (ќФ'/4) S, but we computed D = 0.72567, while ќФ'/4 = 0.4/4=0.1, and S we computed as? S = Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y. For our numeric: Y=1.58745, (1+ќФ)=2, ќФ=1, so first term = 1.58745*2/1 = 3.1749. Second term: ќФ=1, (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)=1+1+0.16=2.16, (2+ќФ)=3, so second term = 1*2.16*3/1.58745 = 6.48/1.58745 = 4.078. So S = 3.1749+4.078=7.2529. Then ќФ'/4 * S = 0.1*7.2529=0.72529. That matches D. Good. So our expression for D is correct.

Now, we computed R = 0.4277, |v| = 1.697, so R|v| = 0.4277*1.697=0.726, which matches D. So we have D = R|v|. That means that our identity S = 4 R |v| / ќФ' must hold. Let's check with numeric: ќФ'=0.4, R=0.4277, |v|=1.697, so 4 R |v|/ќФ' = 4*0.4277*1.697/0.4 = 4*0.726/0.4 = 2.904/0.4 = 7.26. That is close to S=7.2529. So the identity holds numerically. So our algebraic derivation of S^2 = ... should be consistent. But our earlier symbolic manipulation gave a different result. So there must be an error in the symbolic simplification. Let's redo the algebra step by step for S^2 and RHS.

We have:

S = Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.
LetвАЩs denote:

U = Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ, V = ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.
Then S = U+V.

We also have Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So we can write:

U^2 = Y^2 (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ^2 = (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ.
V^2 = ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / Y^2 = ќФ^2 (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / [ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)] = ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2).
2UV = 2 * (Y(1+ќФ)/ќФ) * (ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y) = 2 (1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ).

Thus, S^2 = (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) + 2 (1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ).

Now, factor (2+ќФ) maybe:

S^2 = (2+ќФ) [ (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2/(1-ќФ'^2) + 2 (1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) ].

That is S^2 = (2+ќФ) * Q, where Q = (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ќФ'^2)^2/(1-ќФ'^2) + 2 (1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2).

Now, the right side we need is: RHS = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2-ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ (1+ќФ)^2 + ќФ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)/(1-ќФ'^2) ] = (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ], where A=(1+ќФ)^2, B=ќФ'^2.

We want to show that S^2 = RHS, i.e., (2+ќФ) Q = (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ] => Q = (A-B)/ќФ * [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ].

Now, let's compute Q and the right side symbolically. Write:

Q = (1-B)A/ќФ + ќФ (1+ќФ+ B)^2/(1-B) + 2A(1+ќФ+ B?) Wait, 2 (1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+ќФ'^2) = 2(1+ќФ)(1+ќФ+B) = 2A(1+ќФ+B)? No, A = (1+ќФ)^2, so (1+ќФ) = sqrt(A). Not simple.

Better to compute Q directly using the expressions in terms of ќФ and B. LetвАЩs set:

X = 1+ќФ. Then A = X^2. Also, 1+ќФ+ќФ'^2 = X + B. So:

Q = (1-B)X^2/ќФ + ќФ (X+B)^2/(1-B) + 2X(X+B).

Now, note that ќФ = X-1. So we can write everything in terms of X and B. Then:

Q = (1-B)X^2/(X-1) + (X-1) (X+B)^2/(1-B) + 2X(X+B).

RHS = (X^2 - B)/(X-1) * [ X^2 + (X-1) B (X+1)/(1-B) ]? Because ќФ = X-1, and (2+ќФ) = 2+ (X-1) = X+1. So the RHS factor (2+ќФ)(A-B)/ќФ becomes (X+1)(X^2-B)/(X-1). And the bracket [ A + ќФ B (2+ќФ)/(1-B) ] becomes [ X^2 + (X-1) B (X+1)/(1-B) ]. So RHS = (X+1)(X^2-B)/(X-1) * [ X^2 + (X-1)(X+1)B/(1-B) ].

Thus, we need to show:

(1-B)X^2/(X-1) + (X-1)(X+B)^2/(1-B) + 2X(X+B) = (X+1)(X^2-B)/(X-1) * [ X^2 + (X-1)(X+1)B/(1-B) ].

Now, this is an identity in X and B (with X>1, 0<B<1). We can try to verify by cross-multiplying or simplifying. Since we know it holds numerically, it should be true algebraically. We can try to manipulate.

Multiply both sides by (X-1)(1-B) to clear denominators. Let's do that.

Let LHS multiplied by (X-1)(1-B): 

LHS1 = [ (1-B)X^2/(X-1) + (X-1)(X+B)^2/(1-B) + 2X(X+B) ] * (X-1)(1-B) = (1-B)X^2 * (1-B) + (X-1)(X+B)^2 * (X-1) + 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B). Because:

First term: (1-B)X^2/(X-1) * (X-1)(1-B) = (1-B)X^2 (1-B) = X^2 (1-B)^2.
Second term: (X-1)(X+B)^2/(1-B) * (X-1)(1-B) = (X-1)^2 (X+B)^2.
Third term: 2X(X+B) * (X-1)(1-B) = 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B).

So LHS1 = X^2 (1-B)^2 + (X-1)^2 (X+B)^2 + 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B).

Now, RHS multiplied by (X-1)(1-B): 

RHS1 = (X+1)(X^2-B)/(X-1) * [ X^2 + (X-1)(X+1)B/(1-B) ] * (X-1)(1-B) = (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) * [ X^2 + (X-1)(X+1)B/(1-B) ] = (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) X^2 + (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) * (X-1)(X+1)B/(1-B) = (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) X^2 + (X+1)^2 (X^2-B) B.

Thus, RHS1 = X^2 (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) + B (X+1)^2 (X^2-B).

Now, we need to show that LHS1 = RHS1. That is:

X^2 (1-B)^2 + (X-1)^2 (X+B)^2 + 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B) = X^2 (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) + B (X+1)^2 (X^2-B).

Now, this is a polynomial identity in X and B. Let's expand both sides and simplify.

First, note that X and B are independent. We can try to see if both sides are equal to something like (X^2-B)(something). Let's compute LHS1.

LHS1 = X^2 (1 - 2B + B^2) + (X-1)^2 (X^2 + 2XB + B^2) + 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B).

Compute each term.

Term1: X^2 (1 - 2B + B^2) = X^2 - 2B X^2 + B^2 X^2.

Term2: (X-1)^2 = X^2 - 2X +1. So (X-1)^2 (X^2+2XB+B^2) = (X^2 - 2X +1)(X^2+2XB+B^2). Expand:

Multiply (X^2)(X^2+2XB+B^2) = X^4 + 2X^3 B + X^2 B^2.
(-2X)(X^2+2XB+B^2) = -2X^3 -4X^2 B -2X B^2.
(1)(X^2+2XB+B^2) = X^2 +2X B + B^2.
Sum: X^4 + 2X^3 B + X^2 B^2 -2X^3 -4X^2 B -2X B^2 + X^2 +2X B + B^2.

Combine like terms:
X^4.
X^3 terms: 2X^3 B - 2X^3 = 2X^3(B-1).
X^2 terms: X^2 B^2 -4X^2 B + X^2 = X^2 (B^2 -4B +1).
X terms: -2X B^2 +2X B = 2X B(1 - B).
Constant: B^2.

So Term2 = X^4 + 2X^3(B-1) + X^2(B^2 -4B +1) + 2X B(1-B) + B^2.

Term3: 2X(X+B)(X-1)(1-B). Compute (X+B)(X-1) = X^2 - X + BX - B = X^2 + (B-1)X - B. So Term3 = 2X (1-B) (X^2 + (B-1)X - B) = 2X(1-B)X^2 + 2X(1-B)(B-1)X - 2X(1-B)B = 2X^3(1-B) + 2X^2(1-B)(B-1) - 2X B(1-B). Now, (1-B)(B-1) = -(1-B)^2. So Term3 = 2X^3(1-B) - 2X^2(1-B)^2 - 2X B(1-B).

Thus, LHS1 = Term1 + Term2 + Term3.

Term1: X^2 - 2B X^2 + B^2 X^2.
Term2: X^4 + 2X^3(B-1) + X^2(B^2 -4B +1) + 2X B(1-B) + B^2.
Term3: 2X^3(1-B) - 2X^2(1-B)^2 - 2X B(1-B).

Now, combine terms.

X^4 term: X^4.
X^3 terms: from Term2: 2X^3(B-1); from Term3: 2X^3(1-B). Note that (B-1) = -(1-B), so 2X^3(B-1) = -2X^3(1-B). Then adding Term3's 2X^3(1-B) gives 0. So X^3 terms cancel.
X^2 terms: from Term1: X^2 - 2B X^2 + B^2 X^2.
From Term2: X^2(B^2 -4B +1).
From Term3: -2X^2(1-B)^2.
Sum X^2 terms: X^2 [1 - 2B + B^2 + B^2 -4B +1 - 2(1 - 2B + B^2)] = X^2 [ (1+1) + (-2B -4B) + (B^2+B^2) - 2 +4B -2B^2 ]? Let's compute step by step:

Inside brackets: 1 - 2B + B^2 + B^2 -4B +1 = 2 -6B + 2B^2. Then subtract 2(1 - 2B + B^2) = 2 -4B + 2B^2. So difference: (2 -6B +2B^2) - (2 -4B +2B^2) = -2B. So X^2 terms sum to -2B X^2.
X terms: from Term2: 2X B(1-B); from Term3: -2X B(1-B). They cancel.
Constant term: from Term2: B^2.
Thus, LHS1 = X^4 - 2B X^2 + B^2.

So LHS1 = X^4 - 2B X^2 + B^2 = (X^2 - B)^2? Since (X^2 - B)^2 = X^4 - 2B X^2 + B^2. Yes! So LHS1 = (X^2 - B)^2.

Now, compute RHS1: X^2 (X+1)(X^2-B)(1-B) + B (X+1)^2 (X^2-B). Factor (X^2-B):

RHS1 = (X^2-B) [ X^2 (X+1)(1-B) + B (X+1)^2 ] = (X^2-B) (X+1) [ X^2 (1-B) + B (X+1) ].

Now, compute inside: X^2 (1-B) + B (X+1) = X^2 - B X^2 + B X + B = X^2 + B X + B - B X^2 = X^2 + B X + B (1 - X^2). Not factorable. But we can also write it as X^2 + B(X+1) - B X^2 = X^2 + B(X+1) - B X^2 = X^2 (1-B) + B (X+1). So that's it.

Now, we need to show that (X^2 - B)^2 = (X^2-B)(X+1)[X^2(1-B)+B(X+1)] => if X^2-B вЙ† 0, we can divide both sides by (X^2-B) to get:

X^2 - B = (X+1)[X^2(1-B)+B(X+1)].

Now, check if this identity holds. For numeric: X=2, B=0.16, left side: 4-0.16=3.84. Right side: (2+1)[4*(1-0.16)+0.16*3] = 3[4*0.84+0.48] = 3[3.36+0.48]=3*3.84=11.52. Not equal. We need a systematic algebraic proof.

Maybe we can compute the equation of the circle (BEF) in terms of the coordinates of B, E, F and then compute the distance from H to the line through H direction v? Wait we need to prove that the line through H with direction v is tangent to (BEF). That is equivalent to saying that the line L: (x,y) = H + t v is tangent to (BEF). This can be proven by showing that the quadratic equation in t for intersection has a double root. So if we compute the equation of the circle (BEF), we can substitute (x,y) = H + t v, get a quadratic in t, and show that its discriminant is zero. That is a condition that can be checked algebraically without explicitly computing the center.

So we need to find the equation of the circle through B, E, F. There is a standard method: The general equation of a circle is x^2 + y^2 + Dx + Ey + F = 0. Since B, E, F satisfy it, we can determine D, E, F up to scaling. Then we can substitute the parametric line.

But we also need to use the fact that the circle passes through B, E, F. That gives three linear equations in D, E, F (since the equation is quadratic but we can use that the points satisfy the circle equation, which gives linear equations in D, E, F after subtracting the equation of the circle? Actually, for a circle equation x^2+y^2+Dx+Ey+F=0, plugging a point (x_i,y_i) gives x_i^2+y_i^2 + D x_i + E y_i + F = 0. So we get three linear equations in D, E, F. We can solve for D, E, F in terms of the coordinates. Then we can compute the discriminant condition for the line.

Alternatively, we can use the condition for tangency: The line L is tangent to circle (BEF) if and only if the power of H with respect to (BEF) equals the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency along L, but that is not simpler.

Better: Use the fact that if a line L passes through H and is tangent to circle (BEF), then the equation of L is the polar of H with respect to (BEF)? Actually, the polar of a point H with respect to a circle is the line consisting of points X such that the power of H with respect to the circle equals the square of the distance from H to the line? Wait, for a point H, the polar line is the line such that if you draw any line through H intersecting the circle at two points, then the intersection points of the tangents at those points lie on the polar. But if H lies on the circle, the polar is the tangent at H. That's not our case because H is not on (BEF) generally (in numeric, H=(0.6,-0.3), distance to O=(0.5,-1) = sqrt((0.1)^2+(0.7)^2)= sqrt(0.05+0.49)= sqrt(0.54)=0.735, radius=0.2236, so H outside). So the polar of H w.r.t. (BEF) is a line L' such that if we take the line through H with direction v, it is tangent if and only if that line is exactly the polar? Not exactly: The polar of H is the line consisting of points X such that the power of H with respect to the circle equals the square of the distance from H to the line? Actually, the polar of H is the line that is the locus of points X such that the line through H and X is tangent to the circle? That's the definition: The polar of a point H with respect to a circle is the line containing the points of intersection of the tangents from H to the circle? More precisely, for a given circle and a point H (not on the circle), draw the two tangents from H to the circle touching at T1 and T2. Then the line T1T2 is the polar of H. Also, for any line through H intersecting the circle at P and Q, the intersection of the tangents at P and Q lies on the polar. So if we have a line through H that is tangent to the circle, then the point of tangency is on the circle, and the polar of H passes through that point? Actually, if a line through H is tangent, then H is outside, and the point of tangency is the unique point where the line touches. In that case, the polar of H is the line through the point of tangency that is the chord of contact? But the chord of contact from H is the line joining the two points of tangency from H. If H is outside, there are two tangents, so the chord of contact is the line joining the two points of tangency. If the line through H is tangent, then that tangent line touches at a point T. But from H, there are two tangents: one is the line we consider, and the other is some other line. So the chord of contact is the line through the two points of tangency, which is not the tangent line itself. So our line L is one of the tangents from H. So the polar of H is the line joining the two points of tangency, which is a different line. So L is not the polar; it's a tangent from H. So we can't use polar directly.

Nevertheless, we can compute the condition that L is tangent to the circle: If we substitute the parametric line into the circle equation, we get a quadratic in t. For tangency, the discriminant must be zero. So we need to compute that discriminant and show it's zero using the relationships among the points.

Thus we need to compute the circle equation for B, E, F. Since B, E, F are expressed in terms of u, v, ќ±, ќ≤, we can try to compute the coefficients D, E, F in terms of u, v, N. But maybe there is a simpler way: The circle (BEF) might be the circle with diameter something like the segment connecting the projections of A onto something? There is a formula for the condition that a line is tangent to a circle determined by three points. For points B, E, F, the circle equation can be written as the determinant:

| x^2+y^2, x, y, 1 |
| B^2, B_x, B_y, 1 |
| E^2, E_x, E_y, 1 |
| F^2, F_x, F_y, 1 | = 0.

Where B^2 = x_B^2+y_B^2, etc. Then the line L: H + t v is tangent if and only if when we substitute (x,y) = H + t v, the resulting equation in t has a double root. That condition can be expressed as the determinant of a certain matrix being zero. But that's heavy.

Given the time, I think the analytic approach is doable but we need to present it in a structured way, possibly with simplifications.

Let's try to compute the circle (BEF) using coordinates but with exact expressions in terms of ќФ, ќФ'. We have:

LetвАЩs define:

Let ќФ = ѕБ+ѕБ'-1 > 0, ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ > 0, ќФ' < 1.

Then:

x = (1 - (1+ќФ)ќФ')/2
y = (1/2) sqrt(ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2))

Define:

v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2
v_y = -y(1+ќФ)/ќФ

Now compute:

ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2

We have:

ќ± = (u¬Јv)/|v|^2 = -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/(2|v|^2) = -(1+ќФ-ќФ')(2+ќФ)/(4|v|^2)

ќ≤ = ((u-N)¬Јv)/|v|^2 = -(2+ќФ)(ќФ+ќФ'+1)/(4|v|^2)

Now, we also have H = (p_x, y_H) with p_x = (1+ќФ')/2, y_H = p_x(1-p_x)/p_y = (1+ќФ')/2 * (1 - (1+ќФ')/2) / (-y/ќФ) = (1+ќФ')/2 * ((1-ќФ')/2) * (-ќФ/y) = - (1+ќФ')(1-ќФ')ќФ/(4y) = - (1-ќФ'^2)ќФ/(4y). So H = ((1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(4y)).

Now we need to show that line L: H + t v is tangent to circumcircle of B, E, F.

We can attempt to compute the equation of circle (BEF) in terms of u and v. Perhaps we can find that the circle (BEF) is the circle with diameter BH? Or something like that? In numeric, for ѕБ=1, ѕБ'=1.2, we had B=(0.28,-0.96), H=(0.6,-0.3), not diametral. The radius was 0.2236, distance BH = sqrt((0.32)^2+(0.66)^2)= sqrt(0.1024+0.4356)= sqrt(0.538)=0.734, not 2R.

Maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) is the circle through B and the two points where the line through A and P meets the circles again. There might be a homothety that sends ќ© to ќУ and also sends E to F? Actually, the homothety with center A that sends ќ© to ќУ? Since A is on both circles, there is a homothety with center A that maps ќ© to ќУ? For two intersecting circles, the homothety at A that sends M to N? But the scale factor would be R/r? However, A is not the center of similarity for the circles because the circles intersect at A, and the homothety at A that maps one circle to the other would send the other intersection point B to itself? Actually, if we have two circles intersecting at A and B, then the homothety with center A that sends one circle to the other would send B to some point? But B is also on both circles, so if the homothety sends ќ© to ќУ, then B (on ќ©) must map to some point on ќУ. Since B is also on ќУ, it could map to itself if the homothety fixes B, but then the center would be A and the scale factor would be 1, which would imply the circles coincide. So there is no homothety with center A that sends ќ© to ќУ unless the circles are tangent at A. So not.

Maybe we can consider the inversion with center A that swaps ќ© and ќУ. For intersecting circles, the inversion with center A and power equal to the product of distances to the other intersection? That inversion would map ќ© to ќУ? Actually, an inversion with center A that maps ќ© to ќУ would send the other intersection B to itself? Since B is on both circles, it would be fixed if the inversion radius squared = AB * something? Not sure.

Consider the inversion with center A and radius sqrt(AB * something). This might send M to N? Not.

Given the difficulty, perhaps we can use complex numbers and treat the circles as lines? Might be simpler.

Let's use complex numbers with M=0, N=1 after scaling. Then ќ©: |z|=ѕБ, ќУ: |z-1|=ѕБ'. A is a point on both, so |A|=ѕБ, |A-1|=ѕБ'. Let B = \bar{A} (since reflection across real axis). Then A and B are symmetric.

Now, C = -ѕБ (since C is on ќ© on the side opposite N from M). D = 1+ѕБ' (real). P = circumcenter of A, C, D. In complex numbers, the circumcenter of points a, c, d is given by formula: (a|c|^2(d-c) + c|a|^2(d-c) + d|a|^2(c-a)?? Actually, the circumcenter in complex plane can be computed as:

LetвАЩs recall: For points z1,z2,z3, the circumcenter is:

z0 = ( (z1|z2|^2(z3 - z2) + z2|z3|^2(z1 - z3) + z3|z1|^2(z2 - z1) ) ) / ( z1(z3 - z2) + z2(z1 - z3) + z3(z2 - z1) )? That's messy.

But we might use that P lies on the perpendicular bisector of CD, which is vertical line through O = (C+D)/2 = (-ѕБ+1+ѕБ')/2 = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2. So P has real part = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2. Also, P lies on perpendicular bisector of AC, so |P-A|=|P-C|. That gives equation.

We already derived p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2, p_y = -y/ќФ. In complex, P = p_x + i p_y.

Now, line AP: through A and P. The second intersections: E = A + t_E (P-A) with t_E such that |E|=ѕБ. Since A is on ќ©, and the line through A and P is not necessarily through the center M, but we can compute using complex geometry. Similarly for F.

Now, H = orthocenter of triangle PMN. Since M=0, N=1, P = p_x + i p_y. The orthocenter of triangle with vertices 0,1,P. There is a known formula: For triangle with vertices z1,z2,z3, the orthocenter is z1+z2+z3 - 2z0, where z0 is the circumcenter? Actually, the relation: The circumcenter O, the orthocenter H, and the centroid G satisfy: H = 3G - 2O? Wait, Euler line: O, G, H are collinear with G dividing OH in ratio 1:2 (OG:GH = 1:2). So H = 3G - 2O. Also, G = (z1+z2+z3)/3. So H = z1+z2+z3 - 2O. That is a nice relation: For any triangle, the orthocenter is the sum of the vertices minus twice the circumcenter. So if we can find the circumcenter O_PMN, then H = P + M + N - 2 O_PMN = P + 0 + 1 - 2 O_PMN = P + 1 - 2 O_PMN.

Thus H = P + 1 - 2 O_PMN. So we need to find O_PMN. In triangle with vertices 0,1,P, the circumcenter is the intersection of perpendicular bisectors. Since 0 and 1 are on real axis, the perpendicular bisector of 0 and 1 is the vertical line x=1/2. So O_PMN = (1/2, y0). We can find y0 from condition that O_PMN is equidistant from 0 and P. So |O - 0|^2 = |O - P|^2. That gives (1/2)^2 + y0^2 = (1/2 - p_x)^2 + (y0 - p_y)^2. Solve for y0. This gives a linear equation in y0. Indeed:

(1/4 + y0^2) = (1/2 - p_x)^2 + y0^2 - 2 y0 p_y + p_y^2 => Cancel y0^2: 1/4 = (1/2 - p_x)^2 - 2 y0 p_y + p_y^2 => 2 y0 p_y = (1/2 - p_x)^2 + p_y^2 - 1/4 => y0 = [ (1/2 - p_x)^2 + p_y^2 - 1/4 ] / (2 p_y). Then H = (p_x, p_y) + (1,0) - 2(1/2, y0) = (p_x+1-1, p_y - 2 y0) = (p_x, p_y - 2 y0). But we already have H = (p_x, p_x(1-p_x)/p_y). So we can verify that p_y - 2 y0 = p_x(1-p_x)/p_y. That gives a relation that must hold given the expressions for p_x,p_y. This can be used to simplify later.

Now, we want to prove that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circle BEF. The direction of AP is v = P - A. So L: H + t v.

Now, we can use complex numbers to compute the tangency condition. For a circle through points B, E, F, the condition that line L is tangent can be expressed as the fact that the cross ratio of some points is real? Or we can compute the power of H with respect to the circle and also compute the distance from H to the line L? Not.

Another approach: Show that the circle (BEF) is the reflection of the circle (A C D) across some line? Since P is circumcenter of ACD, the circle (ACD) has center P. The line through H parallel to AP might be the line through H that is the reflection of AP across something. Or perhaps the circle (BEF) is the circle with diameter BH? Let's test with numeric: For ѕБ=1, ѕБ'=1.2, B=(0.28,-0.96), H=(0.6,-0.3). The circle with diameter BH: center at ((0.28+0.6)/2=0.44, (-0.96-0.3)/2=-0.63), radius = 0.5*sqrt((0.32)^2+(0.66)^2)=0.5*0.734=0.367. That's not 0.2236. So no.

Maybe the circle (BEF) is the nine-point circle of triangle ACD? The nine-point circle of triangle ACD passes through the midpoints of its sides and the feet of its altitudes. The circumcenter of ACD is P. The nine-point center is the midpoint of P and the orthocenter of ACD. Not obviously related.

Given the algebra, I think it's feasible to compute the equation of the circle (BEF) in terms of A and v and then check the tangency condition. We have expressions for B, E, F in terms of u, v, ќ±, ќ≤. We can compute the circumcircle equation using determinant or using the fact that the circle through B, E, F can be represented as the set of points X such that (X - B)¬Ј(X - something)? Not.

Maybe we can find that the circle (BEF) is actually the circle through B and the two points where the line through A and P meets the circles again. There might be a relation: Since A, E, F are collinear on v, and B is the reflection of A across the x-axis, the circle (BEF) might be the circle with center at the reflection of something across the x-axis. For instance, consider the circle (A E F) is degenerate (line). But maybe the circle through B, E, F is the circle with diameter BH' where H' is the reflection of H across the x-axis? Not.

Given the complexity, I will try to compute the tangency condition using analytic geometry and symbolic simplification, but present it in a clear, step-by-step manner. Since the problem is an olympiad problem, there should be a synthetic solution, but I can produce an analytic proof that is rigorous. However, the algebra might be long, but we can do it.

Let's proceed with the analytic proof.

We set coordinate system: M=(0,0), N=(1,0). Let the circles be:

ќ©: x^2 + y^2 = ѕБ^2
ќУ: (x-1)^2 + y^2 = ѕБ'^2, with ѕБ' > ѕБ > 0, and they intersect at two points A and B. We take A in the upper half-plane: A=(x_A, y_A) with y_A>0. Then B=(x_A, -y_A). Also, from the intersection conditions:

x_A^2 + y_A^2 = ѕБ^2  (1)
(x_A-1)^2 + y_A^2 = ѕБ'^2  (2)

Subtract (2)-(1): (x_A-1)^2 - x_A^2 = ѕБ'^2 - ѕБ^2 => -2x_A+1 = ѕБ'^2-ѕБ^2 => x_A = (1 - (ѕБ'^2-ѕБ^2))/2 = (1 - ѕБ'^2+ѕБ^2)/2. So x_A = (ѕБ^2 - ѕБ'^2 + 1)/2.

Now, C is the intersection of ќ© with line MN (the x-axis) on the side opposite N. Since M=(0,0) and N=(1,0), the ray from M to N is positive x-direction. The point C is on ќ© such that M is between C and N. So C = (-ѕБ, 0). Similarly, D is the intersection of ќУ with the x-axis on the side opposite M, beyond N. So D = (1+ѕБ', 0).

Thus, points:

C = (-ѕБ, 0)
D = (1+ѕБ', 0)
M = (0,0)
N = (1,0)

Now, define P = circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since C and D lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line through midpoint O = (C+D)/2 = ((-ѕБ)+(1+ѕБ'))/2 = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2. So P has x-coordinate p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2. Also, P lies on perpendicular bisector of AC. The condition PA = PC gives:

|P - A|^2 = |P - C|^2.

Let P = (p_x, p_y). Then:

(p_x - x_A)^2 + (p_y - y_A)^2 = (p_x + ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2.

Expand: p_x^2 - 2p_x x_A + x_A^2 + p_y^2 - 2p_y y_A + y_A^2 = p_x^2 + 2p_x ѕБ + ѕБ^2 + p_y^2.

Cancel p_x^2, p_y^2. Using x_A^2+y_A^2 = ѕБ^2:

-2p_x x_A - 2p_y y_A + ѕБ^2 = 2p_x ѕБ + ѕБ^2 => -2p_x x_A - 2p_y y_A = 2p_x ѕБ => p_y y_A = -p_x x_A - p_x ѕБ = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ). Thus,

p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A.   (3)

Now, we can express x_A+ѕБ in terms of ѕБ,ѕБ'. Since x_A = (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1)/2, then x_A+ѕБ = (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1+2ѕБ)/2 = ((ѕБ+1)^2 - ѕБ'^2)/2 = ((ѕБ+1-ѕБ')(ѕБ+1+ѕБ'))/2. Also, p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2.

Now, we also need the expression for y_A^2. From (1): y_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - x_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - ((ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1)/2)^2. This can be simplified as earlier: y_A^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)/4, where ќФ = ѕБ+ѕБ'-1, ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ. But we can keep it in terms of ѕБ,ѕБ'.

Now, define v = P - A = (p_x - x_A, p_y - y_A). We have:

v_x = p_x - x_A = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2 - (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1)/2 = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ - ѕБ^2+ѕБ'^2-1)/2 = (ѕБ'-ѕБ - ѕБ^2+ѕБ'^2)/2 = (ѕБ'-ѕБ)(1+ѕБ'+ѕБ)/2 = ќФ' (1+ѕБ'+ѕБ)/2.

And v_y = p_y - y_A = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A - y_A = - (p_x (x_A+ѕБ) + y_A^2)/y_A.

We can compute p_x (x_A+ѕБ) + y_A^2 =? Using p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2, x_A+ѕБ = ( (ѕБ+1)^2 - ѕБ'^2 )/2. So p_x (x_A+ѕБ) = ((1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2)*(((ѕБ+1)^2-ѕБ'^2)/2) = ((1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)((ѕБ+1)^2-ѕБ'^2))/4. And y_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - x_A^2. It might be simpler to compute v_y using our earlier expression: v_y = -y_A (1+ѕБ+ѕБ')/ќФ? Actually we derived v_y = -y_A (1+ќФ)/ќФ? Let's recall: v = (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -y_A(1+ќФ)/ќФ). Where ќФ = ѕБ+ѕБ'-1, ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ. That is a nice expression. Let's derive it.

We have:

p_x = (1+ќФ')/2, with ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ.
x_A = (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1)/2 = ( (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2) +1 )/2. But we can also express x_A in terms of ќФ,ќФ'. Since ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2, ѕБ' = (1+ќФ+ќФ')/2. Then x_A = (ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2+1)/2 = ( (ѕБ-ѕБ')(ѕБ+ѕБ') +1 )/2 = ( (-ќФ')( (2ѕБ+ќФ')? Actually, ѕБ+ѕБ' = (1+ќФ-ќФ'+1+ќФ+ќФ')/2 = (2+2ќФ)/2 = 1+ќФ. So ѕБ+ѕБ' = 1+ќФ. And ѕБ-ѕБ' = -ќФ'. So ѕБ^2-ѕБ'^2 = (ѕБ-ѕБ')(ѕБ+ѕБ') = -ќФ'(1+ќФ). Then x_A = (-ќФ'(1+ќФ)+1)/2 = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2. So x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2. Then p_x = (1+ќФ')/2. So v_x = p_x - x_A = (1+ќФ')/2 - (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2 = (1+ќФ' -1 + ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2 = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2. Good.

Now, we need v_y. We have p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. But we also have expression for p_y from earlier: p_y = -y_A/ќФ. Let's verify: From (3): p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. Now, x_A+ѕБ =? Using x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2, and ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2. So x_A+ѕБ = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ) + 1+ќФ-ќФ')/2 = (2 + ќФ - ќФ'(1+ќФ+1?) Actually, compute: 1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ) + 1+ќФ-ќФ' = 2 + ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ'(1+ќФ) = 2+ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ = 2+ќФ -2ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ. That doesn't look like (1+ќФ)^2? Better to use the earlier factorization: x_A+ѕБ = ((1+ѕБ)^2 - ѕБ'^2)/2. And ѕБ' = ѕБ+ќФ', so (1+ѕБ)^2 - (ѕБ+ќФ')^2 = 1+2ѕБ+ѕБ^2 - (ѕБ^2+2ѕБќФ'+ќФ'^2) = 1+2ѕБ-2ѕБќФ'-ќФ'^2 = 1+2ѕБ(1-ќФ')-ќФ'^2. Not nice.

Instead, we can derive p_y from the condition that P lies on perpendicular bisector of AC, which gave p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. Also, from the condition that P lies on perpendicular bisector of AD, we would get the same. Now, we can compute p_x (x_A+ѕБ) using the expressions in terms of ќФ,ќФ' and y_A. We also know that y_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - x_A^2. Let's compute p_x (x_A+ѕБ) in terms of ќФ,ќФ', y_A.

We have p_x = (1+ќФ')/2, x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2. So x_A+ѕБ =? But we also have ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2. So x_A+ѕБ = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ) + 1+ќФ-ќФ')/2 = (2 + ќФ - ќФ'(1+ќФ+1? Actually, 1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ) + 1+ќФ-ќФ' = 2 + ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ'(1+ќФ) = 2+ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ = 2+ќФ -2ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ. That is messy.

Better: Use the earlier derived result: p_y = -y_A/ќФ. Let's verify using the condition that P is circumcenter of ACD. Since C and D are on x-axis, we have that P is on the perpendicular bisector of CD, which is vertical line x = p_x. Also, the circumcenter of ACD is the intersection of the perpendicular bisectors of AC and AD. There is a known fact: For triangle with vertices A, C, D, if we let O be the midpoint of CD, then the circumcenter lies on the line through O perpendicular to CD (which is vertical). Moreover, the distance from P to O is related to the distances from A to the line. We can compute p_y by using that the power of A with respect to the circle with diameter? Not.

Alternatively, we can compute p_y from the fact that the circle (ACD) has center P. The radius squared is |P-C|^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2. Also, since A lies on that circle, we have |P-A|^2 = (p_x - x_A)^2 + (p_y - y_A)^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2. This gave p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. So that is the expression. Now we can also compute |P-D|^2 = (p_x - (1+ѕБ'))^2 + p_y^2. Since D is on the circle, this equals the same radius. That gives (p_x - (1+ѕБ'))^2 + p_y^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2 => (p_x - (1+ѕБ'))^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 => either p_x - (1+ѕБ') = p_x+ѕБ or p_x - (1+ѕБ') = -(p_x+ѕБ). The first gives -1-ѕБ' = ѕБ => ѕБ+ѕБ' = -1, impossible. The second gives p_x - (1+ѕБ') = -p_x - ѕБ => 2p_x = 1+ѕБ' - ѕБ => p_x = (1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2, which is consistent. So that's fine.

Now we need to find p_y in a simpler form. Let's compute p_x (x_A+ѕБ) using the expressions in terms of ќФ,ќФ' and y_A. We have:

p_x = (1+ќФ')/2.
x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2.
ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2.

So x_A+ѕБ = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ) + 1+ќФ-ќФ')/2 = (2 + ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2 = (2 + ќФ - ќФ' - ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ)/2 = (2 + ќФ - 2ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ)/2.

Then p_x (x_A+ѕБ) = ((1+ќФ')/2) * (2 + ќФ - 2ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ)/2 = (1+ќФ')(2 + ќФ - 2ќФ' - ќФ'ќФ)/4.

Now, we also have y_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - x_A^2. But perhaps we can find a relation between p_x (x_A+ѕБ) and y_A^2. We know that p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. So p_y^2 = p_x^2 (x_A+ѕБ)^2 / y_A^2. But we also have the radius squared: R_P^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2. Since A is on the circle, we have (p_x - x_A)^2 + (p_y - y_A)^2 = (p_x+ѕБ)^2 + p_y^2. This gave p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. So that's consistent. We might not need p_y explicitly; we can work with p_y in terms of y_A and ќФ, but we already have a nice expression: p_y = -y_A/ќФ. Let's verify that this expression satisfies the equation p_y = -p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A. That would require:

y_A/ќФ = p_x (x_A+ѕБ)/y_A => y_A^2 = ќФ p_x (x_A+ѕБ). So if we can prove that y_A^2 = ќФ p_x (x_A+ѕБ), then p_y = -y_A/ќФ is consistent. So let's check if y_A^2 = ќФ p_x (x_A+ѕБ) holds given the definitions.

We have ќФ = ѕБ+ѕБ'-1. We can compute y_A^2 = ѕБ^2 - x_A^2. Also, p_x (x_A+ѕБ) = ((1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2)*(x_A+ѕБ). So we need to show:

ѕБ^2 - x_A^2 = ќФ * ((1+ѕБ'-ѕБ)/2)*(x_A+ѕБ)).

Now, note that B, E, F are three points. Since E and F lie on line v through A, and B is the reflection of A across x-axis, we might try to find the circumcircle of BEF. Let's compute the coordinates of these points using the ќФ,ќФ' parametrization.

Now, B = (x_A, -y_A) = (x_A, -Y/2).

Now, we need to prove that line L: H + t v is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF. The direction of L is v. So L is parallel to v. Since v is a direction, and we have points on v: A, E, F are collinear on v. So v is the line through A and P. So L is a line parallel to v.

Now, note that H is on the vertical line x = p_x = (1+ќФ')/2, and H's y-coordinate is y_H = -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(4 y_A) = -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(4 * (Y/2)) = -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y). So H = ( (1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) ).

Now, we want to show that the distance from the circumcenter of BEF to line L equals the radius of (BEF). That is equivalent to showing that the power of H with respect to (BEF) equals the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency T, but maybe we can use the fact that if we take the line through H parallel to v, then its distance to the center is R if and only if H lies on the polar of something? Not.

Another idea: Since we have expressions for E and F, perhaps the circle (BEF) has a simple equation: (x - something)^2 + (y - something)^2 = something. Could it be that the circle (BEF) is actually the circle with diameter BH? Not.

Let's compute the circumcenter O_BEF using vector geometry. Since we have B, E, F, we can compute O as the intersection of perpendicular bisectors. LetвАЩs compute the midpoint of EF: M_EF = (E+F)/2 = A + ( (ќФ/ѕБ' + ќФ/ѕБ)/2 ) v = A + (ќФ/2)(1/ѕБ' + 1/ѕБ) v. Also, the perpendicular bisector of EF is the line through M_EF perpendicular to v. Since v is a direction, this line can be expressed as { M_EF + s w }, where w is a vector perpendicular to v. The perpendicular bisector of BE: B and E. We can compute its direction perpendicular to BE. The circumcenter is the intersection of these two perpendicular bisectors.

Maybe we can find that O_BEF is the reflection of A across the line through H perpendicular to something? Not.

Given the complexity, we might try to prove tangency by showing that the power of H with respect to the circle (BEF) is equal to the square of the distance from H to the line through H in direction v? But that distance is zero because H lies on L, so the power of H is the square of the distance from H to the point of tangency along L? Actually, if L is tangent, then the point of tangency T is the unique point of intersection of L and the circle. Then the power of H is HT^2 (since H is on L, the tangent from H to the circle is just HT). So we need to show that HT^2 = power of H = |H O|^2 - R^2. But we don't know T directly.

Alternatively, we can compute the distance from H to the circle's center O, and then compute the distance from O to L. The condition for tangency is that the distance from O to L equals R. And that distance is |(O-H) √Ч v| / |v|. So we need to prove:

|(O-H) √Ч v| = R |v|.   (4)

If we can compute O and R in terms of A, v, ѕБ, ѕБ', ќФ, ќФ', then we can verify this identity.

Now, note that B, E, F are points on the circle. Since we have explicit coordinates, we can compute O by solving the linear system from the perpendicular bisectors. But maybe there is a clever way: Since E and F are on line v, the circle (BEF) is the circle that passes through B and the two points on v. The chord EF is a segment on v. The perpendicular bisector of EF is a line perpendicular to v at M_EF. The perpendicular bisector of BE: since B is symmetric to A across x-axis, and E is on v, we might relate.

Consider the transformation: reflection across the x-axis. Under reflection, A вЖФ B, and v? v has components (v_x, v_y). Reflecting across x-axis changes y to -y. So v' = (v_x, -v_y). Since v_y is negative, -v_y is positive. The line v after reflection becomes line through B with direction v'? Actually, reflection of the line v (through A with direction v) is the line through B with direction (v_x, -v_y). But note that v_y = -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ). So -v_y = Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) >0. So v' = (v_x, Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)). Also, note that the reflection of E is? E = A + (ќФ/ѕБ') v. Under reflection, AвЖФB, vвЖФv', so the reflection of E is B + (ќФ/ѕБ') v'. But is that point on the circle? Possibly the circle (BEF) is symmetric to some other circle? Not.

Given the algebraic simplifications we've achieved, we can now compute O_BEF explicitly using coordinates but with symbolic simplification. Let's attempt to compute O by solving for the circumcenter using the formula for circumcenter of three points. There is a formula using determinants. But we can use vector algebra: The circumcenter O is given by:

O = ( (|B|^2 (E - F) + |E|^2 (F - B) + |F|^2 (B - E) ) ) / ( 2 (B √Ч E + E √Ч F + F √Ч B) )? That's for 2D using cross product? Actually, for points with coordinates, the circumcenter can be found by solving:

(O - B)¬Ј(E - F) = (|E|^2 - |F|^2)/2? Not.

Better: Use that O is the unique point such that |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2 = |O-F|^2. So O satisfies:

|O|^2 - 2 O¬ЈB + |B|^2 = |O|^2 - 2 O¬ЈE + |E|^2 => 2 O¬Ј(E - B) = |E|^2 - |B|^2.

Similarly, 2 O¬Ј(F - B) = |F|^2 - |B|^2.

Thus, we have two linear equations in O (since O is a vector). So we can solve for O as:

O = (1/2) * ( (|E|^2 - |B|^2) (F - B)^вК•? Actually, we can solve using linear algebra. LetвАЩs denote:

We have:

O¬Ј(E - B) = (|E|^2 - |B|^2)/2
O¬Ј(F - B) = (|F|^2 - |B|^2)/2

We can treat these as equations for O = (x,y). We can solve by writing the system in matrix form. This is doable if we can compute these dot products in terms of A, v, etc.

But maybe we can find a more elegant synthetic proof. Let's try to see if there is a known configuration: The orthocenter H of triangle PMN, and the line through H parallel to AP. Since P is circumcenter of ACD, and A is on both circles, perhaps the circle (BEF) is the circle with diameter BH? But numeric shows not. However, in the first numeric, we had H=(0.6,-0.3), B=(0.28,-0.96), and the circle radius was 0.2236, distance BH=0.734, BH/2=0.367, not R. So no.

Maybe the circle (BEF) is the nine-point circle of triangle PMN? Let's test: For ѕБ=1, ѕБ'=1.2, triangle PMN: P=(0.6,-0.8), M=(0,0), N=(1,0). Its nine-point circle passes through midpoints of sides: MN midpoint (0.5,0), PM midpoint (0.3,-0.4), PN midpoint (0.8,-0.4). Its center is the midpoint of orthocenter H and circumcenter O_PMN. We computed O_PMN=(0.5,-0.25), H=(0.6,-0.3), so nine-point center = (0.55,-0.275). Radius = half of circumradius = 0.2795. Our circle (BEF) had center (0.5,-1) radius 0.2236, not the same. So not.

Maybe the circle (BEF) is the circle with diameter the projection of H onto something? Not.

Given the time, I'll pursue the analytic proof. We have expressions for B, E, F in terms of A, v, ѕБ, ѕБ', ќФ, ќФ'. We can compute O_BEF using the linear equations. Since we have symbolic expressions, we can compute everything in terms of ќФ, ќФ', Y. Then we can compute the distance from O to L and compare to R. This will be a lot of algebra but manageable with systematic simplifications.

LetвАЩs define:

LetвАЩs use the coordinates with the scaling M=(0,0), N=(1,0). We have:

ќФ = ѕБ+ѕБ'-1 > 0, ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ > 0, ќФ' < 1.
We also have ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2, ѕБ' = (1+ќФ+ќФ')/2.

Define Y = sqrt(ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)). So Y>0.

Then:

x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2
y_A = Y/2

v = (v_x, v_y) where v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, v_y = -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)

Now, compute:

E = A + (ќФ/ѕБ') v = A + (2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ')) v
F = A + (ќФ/ѕБ) v = A + (2ќФ/(1+ќФ-ќФ')) v

Also, B = (x_A, -Y/2)

Now, we need to compute the circumcenter O of triangle BEF. LetвАЩs denote O = (X, Y0) (I'll use capital O for the center). We'll find O by solving:

(O - B)¬Ј(E - F) = (|E|^2 - |F|^2)/2? Actually, from equality of distances: |O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2 gives:

2 O¬Ј(E - B) = |E|^2 - |B|^2. Similarly, 2 O¬Ј(F - B) = |F|^2 - |B|^2.

So we need to compute the dot products of O with the vectors (E-B) and (F-B). Since O is unknown, we can solve for O as the intersection of two lines.

Alternatively, we can use the formula for circumcenter in terms of coordinates. LetвАЩs compute the vectors explicitly.

First, compute E-B and F-B.

We have E = A + ќї v, where ќї = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ').
F = A + ќЉ v, where ќЉ = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

And B = (x_A, -Y/2).

Now, A = (x_A, Y/2). So:

E = (x_A + ќї v_x, Y/2 + ќї v_y)
F = (x_A + ќЉ v_x, Y/2 + ќЉ v_y)
B = (x_A, -Y/2)

Thus:

E - B = (ќї v_x, Y/2 + ќї v_y + Y/2) = (ќї v_x, Y + ќї v_y)
F - B = (ќЉ v_x, Y + ќЉ v_y)

Now, v_y = -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ). So compute Y + ќї v_y = Y + ќї * (-Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)) = Y [1 - ќї (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)].

Similarly, Y + ќЉ v_y = Y [1 - ќЉ (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)].

Now, ќї = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ'). So ќї (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) = (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ'). So 1 - ќї (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) = 1 - (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = ( (1+ќФ+ќФ') - (1+ќФ) )/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ').

Thus, Y + ќї v_y = Y * ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ').

Similarly, ќЉ = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ-ќФ'). Then ќЉ (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) = (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ'). So 1 - ќЉ (1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) = 1 - (1+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ') = ( (1+ќФ-ќФ') - (1+ќФ) )/(1+ќФ-ќФ') = -ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

Thus, Y + ќЉ v_y = Y * ( -ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ') ) = -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

So we have:

E - B = (ќї v_x, Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ'))
F - B = (ќЉ v_x, -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ'))

Now, compute v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2. So ќї v_x = (2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ')) * (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2) = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ))/(1+ќФ+ќФ').

Similarly, ќЉ v_x = (2ќФ/(1+ќФ-ќФ')) * (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2) = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ))/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

Thus:

E - B = ( ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ') , Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ') )
F - B = ( ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ') , -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ') )

Now, we need to compute |E|^2 - |B|^2 and |F|^2 - |B|^2.

We have:

|B|^2 = x_A^2 + (Y/2)^2 = x_A^2 + Y^2/4. Since x_A^2+Y^2/4 = ѕБ^2? Actually, x_A^2 + y_A^2 = ѕБ^2, and y_A = Y/2, so |B|^2 = x_A^2 + Y^2/4 = ѕБ^2.

So |B|^2 = ѕБ^2.

Now, |E|^2 = (x_A+ќї v_x)^2 + (Y/2+ќї v_y)^2. But we can compute |E|^2 - |B|^2 using the fact that A, v, and ќї are known. Alternatively, note that E = A + ќї v, and |A|^2 = ѕБ^2, |v|^2 = something, and A¬Јv = -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/2? Actually, we already computed A¬Јv = -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/2. So:

|E|^2 = |A|^2 + 2ќї (A¬Јv) + ќї^2 |v|^2 = ѕБ^2 + 2ќї (A¬Јv) + ќї^2 |v|^2.

Thus, |E|^2 - ѕБ^2 = 2ќї (A¬Јv) + ќї^2 |v|^2.

Similarly, |F|^2 - ѕБ^2 = 2ќЉ (A¬Јv) + ќЉ^2 |v|^2.

Now, we have A¬Јv = -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/2. And |v|^2 = ѕБѕБ'(2+ќФ)/ќФ. So we can compute these.

But maybe we can compute |E|^2 - |B|^2 directly using the expressions we derived for E-B. Since E-B = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ'), Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ')). Then |E-B|^2 = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ'))^2 + (Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ'))^2 = ќФ'^2/(1+ќФ+ќФ')^2 [ ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 + Y^2 ].

Now, note that Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 + Y^2 = ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 + ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) = ќФ(2+ќФ)[ ќФ(2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2) ] = ќФ(2+ќФ)[ ќФ(2+ќФ) + 1 - ќФ'^2 ]. But we might also compute |E-B|^2 in a simpler form later.

Now, we also have that O is the circumcenter, so we need to solve for O from the linear equations. Let's set O = (X, Y0). Then:

2 O¬Ј(E-B) = |E|^2 - |B|^2 = 2ќї (A¬Јv) + ќї^2 |v|^2.
2 O¬Ј(F-B) = |F|^2 - |B|^2 = 2ќЉ (A¬Јv) + ќЉ^2 |v|^2.

But we can also write O¬Ј(E-B) = (|E|^2 - |B|^2)/2, and O¬Ј(F-B) = (|F|^2 - |B|^2)/2.

Now, note that the vectors (E-B) and (F-B) are not orthogonal in general. We can solve for O by representing O as combination of two perpendicular vectors? Actually, we can treat the system as:

[ (E-B)_x, (E-B)_y; (F-B)_x, (F-B)_y ] * O = ( (|E|^2-|B|^2)/2, (|F|^2-|B|^2)/2 )? Wait, O is a vector, and the dot product with (E-B) is a linear equation. So we have two linear equations in the components of O. This is a system of two equations in two unknowns. We can solve by inverting the matrix formed by the vectors (E-B) and (F-B) as rows? Actually, the equations are:

O_x * (E-B)_x + O_y * (E-B)_y = RHS1
O_x * (F-B)_x + O_y * (F-B)_y = RHS2

So the coefficient matrix is M = [ (E-B)_x, (E-B)_y; (F-B)_x, (F-B)_y ]? But careful: The rows are the vectors? Actually, if we write O = (x,y), then the equations are:

x*(E-B)_x + y*(E-B)_y = RHS1
x*(F-B)_x + y*(F-B)_y = RHS2

So the matrix is:

[ (E-B)_x, (E-B)_y ]
[ (F-B)_x, (F-B)_y ]

Thus, we need to solve for (x,y) by inverting this 2x2 matrix. So the determinant is (E-B)_x*(F-B)_y - (E-B)_y*(F-B)_x.

Let's compute that determinant. Denote:

U = (E-B)_x = ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ')
V = (E-B)_y = Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ')
W = (F-B)_x = ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ')
Z = (F-B)_y = -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ')

Then the determinant D = U*Z - V*W = [ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ')] * [ -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ') ] - [Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ')] * [ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ')] = - ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) Y ќФ' / [(1+ќФ+ќФ')(1+ќФ-ќФ')] - Y ќФ' ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ) / [(1+ќФ+ќФ')(1+ќФ-ќФ')] = -2 ќФ ќФ'^2 Y (2+ќФ) / [(1+ќФ+ќФ')(1+ќФ-ќФ')].

Thus, D = -2 ќФ ќФ'^2 Y (2+ќФ) / [(1+ќФ+ќФ')(1+ќФ-ќФ')].

Now, we can solve for O using Cramer's rule. But we need to compute O_x and O_y. However, maybe we don't need O explicitly; we need the distance from O to line L. Since L is parallel to v, the distance from O to L is the absolute value of the component of (O - H) perpendicular to v. That is |(O-H) √Ч v| / |v|. So we need to compute (O-H) √Ч v. Since v is a known direction, we can compute the cross product as the determinant of (O-H) and v. This is a linear expression in O. We can compute O using the formulas for the circumcenter, but maybe we can compute (O-H) √Ч v directly from the conditions that define O.

Recall that O is the circumcenter of BEF. There is a known relation: For any point X, the power of X with respect to circle (BEF) is |X-O|^2 - R^2. Also, the line through H parallel to v is tangent if and only if the power of H equals (distance from H to foot)^2? Actually, if L is tangent, then the point of tangency T is the foot of perpendicular from O to L, and HT^2 = power of H. So we need to show that the distance from O to L equals R. That is equivalent to showing that the foot of perpendicular from O to L is at distance R from O, which is true if and only if the projection of (O-H) onto the direction perpendicular to v has magnitude R, but that's messy.

Another approach: Show that the circle (BEF) is the image of the circle (ACD) under some transformation that sends H to something. Since P is the center of (ACD), and H is the orthocenter of PMN, there might be a homothety centered at A that sends (ACD) to (BEF)? Not exactly.

Let's compute the coordinates of the circumcenter O_BEF in terms of the parameters. We have the linear system. Let's solve for O.

We have:

x = O_x, y = O_y.

Equations:

x U + y V = RHS1
x W + y Z = RHS2

where U, V, W, Z as above.

RHS1 = (|E|^2 - ѕБ^2)/2 = ќї (A¬Јv) + (ќї^2/2) |v|^2. Since A¬Јv = -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/2, |v|^2 = ѕБѕБ'(2+ќФ)/ќФ.

Thus, RHS1 = ќї * ( -ѕБ(2+ќФ)/2 ) + (ќї^2/2) * (ѕБѕБ'(2+ќФ)/ќФ) = -ќї ѕБ (2+ќФ)/2 + (ќї^2 ѕБ ѕБ' (2+ќФ))/(2ќФ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( -ќї + ќї^2 ѕБ' / ќФ ).

Similarly, RHS2 = ќЉ (A¬Јv) + (ќЉ^2/2) |v|^2 = -ќЉ ѕБ (2+ќФ)/2 + (ќЉ^2 ѕБ ѕБ' (2+ќФ))/(2ќФ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( -ќЉ + ќЉ^2 ѕБ' / ќФ ).

Now, note that ќї = 2ќФ/ѕБ'? Actually, ќї = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ') and ѕБ' = (1+ќФ+ќФ')/2, so ќї = 2ќФ/(1+ќФ+ќФ') = (2ќФ)/(2ѕБ') = ќФ/ѕБ'. So ќї = ќФ/ѕБ'. Similarly, ќЉ = ќФ/ѕБ.

Thus, ќї = ќФ/ѕБ', ќЉ = ќФ/ѕБ.

Then compute:

-ќї + ќї^2 ѕБ' / ќФ = - (ќФ/ѕБ') + (ќФ^2/ѕБ'^2) * ѕБ' / ќФ = -ќФ/ѕБ' + ќФ/ѕБ' = 0. So RHS1 = 0! Because -ќї + ќї^2 ѕБ'/ќФ = 0. So (|E|^2 - ѕБ^2)/2 = 0. That means |E|^2 = ѕБ^2. But that is true because E is on ќ©, and |A|=ѕБ, and we have E = A + (ќФ/ѕБ') v. But does that imply |E| = ѕБ? Actually, E is on ќ©, so |E| = ѕБ. So indeed |E|^2 = ѕБ^2. So RHS1 = 0. Similarly, RHS2 = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( -ќЉ + ќЉ^2 ѕБ'/ќФ ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( -ќФ/ѕБ + (ќФ^2/ѕБ^2) * ѕБ'/ќФ ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( -ќФ/ѕБ + ќФ ѕБ'/ѕБ^2 ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( ќФ ( -1/ѕБ + ѕБ'/ѕБ^2 ) ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( ќФ ( ( -ѕБ + ѕБ')/ѕБ^2 ) ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБ/2 * ( ќФ ќФ'/ѕБ^2 ) = (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (2ѕБ). So RHS2 = (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (2ѕБ).

Thus, we have:

2 O¬Ј(E-B) = 0 => O¬Ј(E-B) = 0.
2 O¬Ј(F-B) = RHS2 => O¬Ј(F-B) = RHS2/2 = (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (4ѕБ).

So the equations become:

O_x * U + O_y * V = 0
O_x * W + O_y * Z = (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (4ѕБ)

Now, note that U and V are as above. So the first equation says that O is perpendicular to (E-B) (i.e., O is orthogonal to vector (E-B)). That is, O lies on the line through the origin perpendicular to (E-B). Since (E-B) = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ'), Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ')). So O is orthogonal to that vector, meaning O is in the direction of ( -V, U ) (since dot product zero). So O is a scalar multiple of ( -V, U ) = ( -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ'), ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ') ). So O = k * ( -Y, ќФ (2+ќФ) ) times some factor? Indeed, O = t * ( -Y, ќФ (2+ќФ) ) for some t, because the factor ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ') can be absorbed. Let's compute:

Let O = (x, y). Then from O¬Ј(E-B)=0: x * (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ+ќФ')) + y * (Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ+ќФ')) = 0 => multiply by (1+ќФ+ќФ')/ќФ': x ќФ (2+ќФ) + y Y = 0 => y = - x ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y. So O = (x, - x ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y). So O lies on the line through the origin with direction (1, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/Y). So O = x * (1, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/Y).

Now, we also have the second equation: O¬Ј(F-B) = RHS2/2 = (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (4ѕБ). Compute F-B = (W, Z) = (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ'), -Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ')). So O¬Ј(F-B) = x * W + y * Z = x * (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ')) + y * (-Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ')). Substitute y = - x ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y:

Then O¬Ј(F-B) = x * (ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ')) + (- x ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y) * (-Y ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ')) = x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ') + x ќФ (2+ќФ) ќФ'/(1+ќФ-ќФ') = 2 x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

Thus, O¬Ј(F-B) = 2 x ќФ ќФ' (2+ќФ)/(1+ќФ-ќФ').

Set this equal to (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' / (4ѕБ). Cancel (2+ќФ) ќФ ќФ' (assuming nonzero). Then we get:

2 x / (1+ќФ-ќФ') = 1/(4ѕБ) => x = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/(8ѕБ). But note that ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2, so (1+ќФ-ќФ') = 2ѕБ. Then x = (2ѕБ)/(8ѕБ) = 1/4. So x = 1/4.

Thus, O = (1/4, y) with y = - x ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y = - (1/4) ќФ (2+ќФ)/Y. So O = (1/4, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y)).

Thus, we have found the circumcenter O_BEF: O = (1/4, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y)). And we can compute the radius R = distance from O to B (or E or F). Since we have O and B, we can compute R.

B = (x_A, -Y/2). Recall x_A = (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2. And Y = sqrt(ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)). So we need to compute R^2 = |O - B|^2.

We have O - B = (1/4 - x_A, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y) + Y/2) = (1/4 - x_A, (Y/2) - (ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y))).

Compute 1/4 - x_A = 1/4 - (1 - ќФ'(1+ќФ))/2 = 1/4 - 1/2 + ќФ'(1+ќФ)/2 = -1/4 + ќФ'(1+ќФ)/2 = ( -1 + 2ќФ'(1+ќФ) )/4 = ( 2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1 )/4.

Now, Y/2 - ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y) = (Y^2/2 - ќФ(2+ќФ)/4)/Y? Actually, Y/2 - ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y) = (2Y^2 - ќФ(2+ќФ))/(4Y). Because Y/2 = (2Y^2)/(4Y). So difference = (2Y^2 - ќФ(2+ќФ))/(4Y). Now, Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So 2Y^2 = 2ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). Then 2Y^2 - ќФ(2+ќФ) = ќФ(2+ќФ)[2(1-ќФ'^2) - 1] = ќФ(2+ќФ)[2 - 2ќФ'^2 - 1] = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1 - 2ќФ'^2). So O - B = ( (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)/4 , ќФ(2+ќФ)(1 - 2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ).

Now, we also have H = ( (1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) ). And v = ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ).

Now, we want to prove that the line through H parallel to v is tangent to circle (BEF). That is, the distance from O to line L (through H direction v) equals R. So we need to show:

| (O - H) √Ч v | = R |v|.   (4)

We can compute O-H and v. Since we have explicit expressions, we can compute the cross product (determinant) and then compare to R|v|.

Let's compute O-H and v.

First, O = (1/4, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y)).
H = ((1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y)).

So O - H = (1/4 - (1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y) + ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y)).

Compute first component: 1/4 - (1+ќФ')/2 = (1 - 2(1+ќФ'))/4 = (1 - 2 - 2ќФ')/4 = (-1 - 2ќФ')/4 = -(1+2ќФ')/4.

Second component: -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y) + ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y) = ќФ/Y * ( - (2+ќФ)/4 + (1-ќФ'^2)/2 ) = ќФ/Y * ( - (2+ќФ)/4 + (2(1-ќФ'^2))/4 ) = ќФ/Y * ( ( -2-ќФ + 2 - 2ќФ'^2 )/4 ) = ќФ/Y * ( ( -ќФ - 2ќФ'^2 )/4 ) = -ќФ (ќФ + 2ќФ'^2)/(4Y).

Thus, O-H = ( - (1+2ќФ')/4 , -ќФ (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ).

Now, v = (v_x, v_y) = ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2 , -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ). Write v = ( (2+ќФ)ќФ'/2 , -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ).

We need to compute the cross product (determinant) of (O-H) and v: D = (O-H)_x * v_y - (O-H)_y * v_x.

Compute:

(O-H)_x * v_y = ( - (1+2ќФ')/4 ) * ( -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ) ) = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ) / (8ќФ).

(O-H)_y * v_x = ( -ќФ (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ) * ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2 ) = -ќФ (ќФ+2ќФ'^2) ќФ' (2+ќФ) / (8Y). So (O-H)_y * v_x = -ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y).

Thus, D = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ) - ( -ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y) )? Actually, D = (O-H)_x * v_y - (O-H)_y * v_x = first term - second term. So D = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ) - ( -ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y) ) = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ) + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y).

So D = (1/(8)) [ (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y ].

Now, we need to compute R|v|. First, compute R^2 = |O-B|^2.

We have O-B = ( (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)/4 , ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ). So

R^2 = [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)/4 ]^2 + [ ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ]^2 = (1/16)[ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / Y^2 ].

Now, Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So we can simplify the second term:

ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / Y^2 = ќФ^2 (2+ќФ)^2 (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / [ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)] = ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2).

Thus, R^2 = (1/16)[ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ].

Now, compute |v|^2 = v_x^2+v_y^2 = (ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2)/4 + Y^2 (1+ќФ)^2/(4ќФ^2) = (1/4)[ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2 + (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) * (1+ќФ)^2 / ќФ^2 )? Actually, Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2), so v_y^2 = (Y^2 (1+ќФ)^2)/(4ќФ^2) = (ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) (1+ќФ)^2)/(4ќФ^2) = (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/(4ќФ). So |v|^2 = (ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ)^2)/4 + (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/(4ќФ) = (2+ќФ)/4 [ ќФ'^2 (2+ќФ) + (1-ќФ'^2)(1+ќФ)^2/ќФ ] = (2+ќФ)/4 * (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ? Actually, we earlier simplified T = (1+2ќФ+ќФ^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ = ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ. So |v|^2 = (2+ќФ)/4 * ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ). But ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2) = (1+ќФ-ќФ')(1+ќФ+ќФ') = (2ѕБ)(2ѕБ')? Actually, ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2, ѕБ' = (1+ќФ+ќФ')/2, so (1+ќФ-ќФ')(1+ќФ+ќФ') = 4ѕБѕБ'. So |v|^2 = (2+ќФ) * 4ѕБѕБ' / (4ќФ) = (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ. So |v| = sqrt( (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ ). Good.

Now, we need to show that D = R |v|. That is:

(1/8)[ (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y ] = R * sqrt( (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ ).

We can try to square both sides and simplify. But this is heavy.

Maybe we can find a simpler relation: The line through H parallel to v is tangent to (BEF) if and only if H is the orthocenter of triangle BEF? Let's test numeric: For ѕБ=1, ѕБ'=1.2, we have H=(0.6,-0.3). Triangle BEF: B=(0.28,-0.96), E=(0.6,-0.8), F=(0.664,-1.152). Compute altitudes? Not sure.

Alternatively, note that we found O_BEF = (1/4, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y)). That is a nice expression. Also, H = ((1+ќФ')/2, -ќФ(1-ќФ'^2)/(2Y)). So O-H = ( - (1+2ќФ')/4, -ќФ(ќФ+2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ). Now, v = (ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2, -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)). Perhaps we can compute the vector from O to H projected onto v? But we need the distance from O to L.

Let's compute the distance from O to line L: distance = |(O-H) √Ч v| / |v|. We have D = (O-H) √Ч v. So we need to compute D^2 and compare to R^2 |v|^2.

We already have D expressed as (1/8) times a sum. Let's compute D^2.

First, compute D = (1/8) * S, where S = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.

We can write S = (1+ќФ)/ќФ * (1+2ќФ') Y + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.

Now, we also have R^2 |v|^2 = R^2 * (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ. We can compute R^2 in terms of ќФ, ќФ', Y. Perhaps we can find that D^2 = R^2 |v|^2.

Given the algebraic simplifications we've seen, it's plausible that the identity holds. But we need to present a proof.

We can try to simplify R^2 |v|^2.

We have:

R^2 = (1/16)[ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ].

|v|^2 = (2+ќФ)ѕБѕБ'/ќФ. And ѕБѕБ' = (1+ќФ-ќФ')(1+ќФ+ќФ')/4 = ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/4 = ( (1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2 )/4.

Thus, |v|^2 = (2+ќФ)/ќФ * ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/4 = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ).

So R^2 |v|^2 = (1/16) * (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) * [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ]? Actually, R^2 |v|^2 = R^2 * |v|^2. So:

R^2 |v|^2 = (1/16) * (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) * [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ].

Now, note that ((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2) = (1+ќФ-ќФ')(1+ќФ+ќФ') = 4ѕБѕБ'. But maybe we can combine with the other terms.

Now, compute D^2 = (1/64) S^2. So we need to show that S^2 = 64 R^2 |v|^2. This is equivalent to:

S^2 = 64 * (1/16) * (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) * [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ] = 4 * (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/(4ќФ) * [ ... ] = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ ... ].

So S^2 = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ].

Now, S = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.

We can try to square S and compare. This seems messy but maybe we can use the expression for Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). Then we can rewrite S in terms of Y and ќФ,ќФ'.

Let's denote:

A = (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ)/ќФ * Y
B = ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y

So S = A + B.

Then S^2 = A^2 + B^2 + 2AB.

Now, A^2 = (1+2ќФ')^2 (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ^2 * Y^2 = (1+2ќФ')^2 (1+ќФ)^2/ќФ^2 * ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2) = (1+2ќФ')^2 (1+ќФ)^2 (2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)/ќФ.

Similarly, B^2 = ќФ^2 ќФ'^2 (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / Y^2 = ќФ^2 ќФ'^2 (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ)^2 / [ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2)] = ќФ ќФ'^2 (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)^2 (2+ќФ) / (1-ќФ'^2).

And 2AB = 2 * (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ)/ќФ * Y * ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y = 2 (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ) ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) * (Y/Y) * (ќФ/ќФ? Actually, careful:

A * B = [ (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ)/ќФ * Y ] * [ ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y ] = (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ) ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) * (Y/Y) * (ќФ/ќФ?) Wait, there is a ќФ in denominator of A and a ќФ in numerator of B? A has (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ)/ќФ * Y, B has ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y. So product = (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ) ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ) * (Y/Y) * (ќФ/ќФ)?? Actually, the ќФ cancels: A has /ќФ, B has ќФ, so they cancel. So A*B = (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ) ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ). So 2AB = 2 (1+2ќФ') (1+ќФ) ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ).

Now, we need to show that S^2 equals the expression:

E = (2+ќФ)((1+ќФ)^2 - ќФ'^2)/ќФ * [ (2ќФ'(1+ќФ) - 1)^2 + ќФ (2+ќФ) (1-2ќФ'^2)^2 / (1-ќФ'^2) ].

Multiply both sides by something? This is heavy.

Given the difficulty, I think it's acceptable to present the analytic proof, but we need to ensure that the algebra is correct and can be presented in a concise manner. We can use the expressions we derived to compute the distance from O to L and compare to R. We already computed O-H and v. Let's compute the determinant D = (O-H) √Ч v more explicitly, and also compute R^2 |v|^2. Maybe we can find that D = (something) * R * |v|. Let's compute D in terms of ќФ, ќФ', Y.

We have:

D = (1/(8)) [ (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y ].

Now, note that Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). So we can write:

(1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/ќФ = (1+2ќФ')(1+ќФ)/ќФ * Y.
ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y = ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/Y.

Now, we can try to see if D is proportional to R|v|. Since R|v| =? We can compute R|v|^2 = R^2 |v|^2, but we need R|v|.

Maybe we can compute D^2 and R^2|v|^2 directly and show they are equal using the relation Y^2 = ќФ(2+ќФ)(1-ќФ'^2). This is a polynomial identity in ќФ and ќФ'. Since ќФ and ќФ' are independent? Given the difficulty, perhaps the analytic proof is the way to go, but we need to present it concisely. Since we already derived that O_BEF = (1/4, -ќФ(2+ќФ)/(4Y)), and we have H and v, we can compute the distance from O to L. Maybe we can simplify by factoring.

Let's compute D = (O-H)_x * v_y - (O-H)_y * v_x.

We have:

(O-H)_x = - (1+2ќФ')/4
v_y = -Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)
So first term = (- (1+2ќФ')/4) * (-Y(1+ќФ)/(2ќФ)) = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ)

(O-H)_y = -ќФ(ќФ+2ќФ'^2)/(4Y)
v_x = ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2
So second term = ( -ќФ(ќФ+2ќФ'^2)/(4Y) ) * ( ќФ'(2+ќФ)/2 ) = -ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y). So D = first term - second term = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ) - ( -ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y) ) = (1+2ќФ') Y (1+ќФ)/(8ќФ) + ќФ ќФ' (ќФ+2ќФ'^2)(2+ќФ)/(8Y). Given the time, perhaps we can find a simpler synthetic proof. Let's try to think synthetically.

We have two circles intersecting at A and B. LetвАЩs denote the line through centers MN. Points C and D are defined as above. Let P be circumcenter of triangle ACD. Then PA = PC = PD. So P is equidistant from A, C, D.

The altitude from M is the line through M perpendicular to PN. This line might have some relation to the circle (ACD). 

Another approach: Use coordinates but with a different normalization to simplify the algebra. Instead of setting d=1, we could set the sum of radii or something. Since the circles intersect, an inversion with center at A will send them to two lines that intersect at the image of B. That might simplify. Let's try that.

Plug into Eq2:

Then O_x = (2 Y ѕБ O_y) / ((2+ќФ)ќФ ќФ') = (2 Y ѕБ * (-(2+ќФ)ќФ/(2Y))) / ((2+ќФ)ќФ ќФ') = ( - ѕБ (2+ќФ)ќФ ) / ((2+ќФ)ќФ ќФ') = - ѕБ / ќФ'. So O_x = - ѕБ / ќФ'.

Now, note that ѕБ = (1+ќФ-ќФ')/2, and ќФ' = ѕБ'-ѕБ. So O_x = - (1+ќФ-ќФ')/(2ќФ'). But we also have that X = 1+ќФ. So O_x = - (X - ќФ')/(2ќФ'). That is negative. In our numeric with ѕБ=0.8, ќФ'=0.4, X=2, then O_x = - (2-0.4)/(2*0.4) = -1.6/0.8 = -2. So O_x = -2. But we computed O from solving perpendicular bisectors as x=0.5003, not -2. Given B(0.1, -0.793725)
